Full text: M2 PRESSWIRE-March 29, 2007-bellwetherreport.com: Daily Market Alert for GameStop Corp. (C)1994-2007 M2 COMMUNICATIONS LTD
GameStop holds the top score in the video game retailing industry. The company is the largest retailer of new and used games, hardware, entertainment software, and accessories through nearly 4,500 outlets in the US and 14 other countries. A majority of sales come from new and used video games; stores carry an average of 1,000 new titles and 4,000 used ones. The company also has e-commerce Web sites (GameStop.com, ebgames.com) and publishes Game Informer, a video game magazine that reaches more than 1.5 million subscribers. The company's 2005 purchase of rival Electronics Boutique doubled GameStop's size.
Shares were down 1% retreating from earlier gains.
BellwetherReport.com is a leading online research firm for international investors looking to get an edge over their portfolio. Investors seeking the most up to date information on GameStop Corp. are invited to sign up for a free complimentary subscription to www.bellwetherreport.com. No credit card needed!
Shares of video game publisher Activision Inc. jumped to a 52- week high Wednesday on the heels of a solid fourth-quarter and full- year report from No. 1 game retailer GameStop Inc., whose stock hit a record high for the second day in a row.
Activision, whose games include the "Guitar Hero" and "Tony Hawk" series, is receiving positive early buzz from its third "Spider- Man" title, said Lazard Capital Markets analyst Colin Sebastian in a note to investors.
"Spider-Man 3," the game, is slated to launch in May, simultaneously with the movie.
Activision also continues to reap the benefits of its catalog titles, most notably "Guitar Hero II," which lets players pretend they are rock stars, and the World War II game "Call of Duty." The analyst boosted his fiscal fourth-quarter outlook for Activision, to sales of $225 million from $200 million, and to a net loss of 7 cents per share from a loss of 8 cents. (Video game software publishers make much of their money in the fiscal third quarter due to the holiday shopping season, and often see losses in other quarters.) Shares of the Santa Monica, Calif., company rose 88 cents, or 4.9 percent, to close at $19.01 on the Nasdaq Stock Market. Earlier, shares traded as high as $19.20, eclipsing a previous 52-week high of $18.79.
GameStop's shares, meanwhile, rose $1.44, or 4.6 percent, to end at $32.60 on the New York Stock Exchange. The stock hit its prior, split-adjusted all-time high of $31.43 on Tuesday after the company posted its results.
The company's management called the recent European launch of Sony Corp.'s PlayStation 3 "very good, but not great," Sebastian wrote, adding that this likely means Sony is "coming close to reaching its one million unit shipment target." The PlayStation 3 was launched in the U.S. in November.
The analyst also noted that March video game retail sales might be slightly hurt by short supplies of the Nintendo Wii and Nintendo DS.
Sebastian kept a "Buy" rating on Activision with a target price of $20. He rates GameStop "Buy."

Full text: M2 PRESSWIRE-March 29, 2007-bellwetherreport.com: In- Depth Research on GameStop Corp (C)1994-2007 M2 COMMUNICATIONS LTD
In- Depth Research on GameStop Corp (NYSE:GME)
GameStop Corp. retails video game products and PC entertainment software. The company sells new and used software, hardware, and game accessories for the PC and video game systems from Sony, Nintendo, and Microsoft. It also provides computer and video game magazines and strategy guides, action figures, and other related merchandise. In addition, the company operates electronic commerce Websites under the names gamestop.com and ebgames.com, as well as publishes Game Informer, a multiplatform video game magazine in the United States with approximately 1.9 million subscribers. As of April 10, 2006, it operated 4,490 stores in the United States, Australia, Canada, and Europe primarily under the names GameStop and EB Games. The company was founded in 1994 and is headquartered in Grapevine, Texas.
Shares were up 3% after the video game and software retailer reached an all-time high.
BellwetherReport.com is a leading online research firm for international investors looking to get an edge over their portfolio. Investors seeking the most up to date information on GameStop Corp are invited to sign up for a free complimentary subscription to www.bellwetherreport.com. No credit card needed!
Shares of GameStop Corp. edged higher in Wednesday premarket trading, after the video game and software retailer reached an all- time high Tuesday on a positive fiscal fourth-quarter report and 2007 forecast.
The Grapevine, Texas-based company said net income rose 53 percent on a 38 percent jump in revenue to $2.3 billion, beating Wall Street expectations. For the year ending Feb. 2, 2008, GameStop predicts profit of $1.37 to $1.40 per share and expects to open 500 to 550 stores.
Lazard Capital Markets analyst Colin Sebastian said GameStop's revenue was higher than he anticipated due to stronger hardware sales, and same-store sales also beat his expectations. Sebastian raised his price target to $35 from $30 and reiterated a "Buy" rating on the stock.
"While there are still risks associated with the console transitions and sluggish PS3 and Xbox 360 hardware sales, we believe that overall positive industry trends are likely to continue through at least 2008," he said in a note to clients.
Sebastian added the company's successful merger with Electronics Boutique and better sales and earnings justify investor optimism about GameStop.

Earnings Digest -- Retail: GameStop Corp.

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]28 Mar 2007: C.8.

Full text: GameStop Corp.'s fiscal fourth-quarter results were lifted by strong sales of videogame consoles such as Nintendo Co.'s Wii, Microsoft Corp.'s Xbox 360 and Sony Corp.'s PlayStation 3. The company also said it is in the early stages of another strong growth cycle, helped by a strong release slate of videogame titles across all platforms. GameStop also issued first-quarter and full-year earnings forecasts ahead of Wall Street expectations. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame and entertainment-software retailer's sales in the quarter ended Feb. 3 rose 38% from the year-earlier period. GameStop expects fiscal first- quarter earnings of 15 cents to 16 cents a share, up from net income of $11.7 million, or seven cents a share, a year earlier. Same-store sales, or sales at stores open at least a year, are expected to grow 12% to 14%. GameStop expects fiscal 2008 earnings of $1.37 to $1.40 a share on sales growth of 19% to 21%, with same-store sales rising 14% to 16%. Shares rose $3.19, or 11%, to $31.16 in 4 p.m. New York Stock Exchange composite trading.

Full text: M2 PRESSWIRE-March 27, 2007-bellwetherreport.com: GameStop Corp is Added to the Bellwether Watch list (C)1994-2007 M2 COMMUNICATIONS LTD
GameStop Corp. (NYSE:GME) is Added to the Bellwether Watch list
GameStop Corp. retails video game products and PC entertainment software. The company sells new and used software, hardware, and game accessories for the PC and video game systems from Sony, Nintendo, and Microsoft. It also provides computer and video game magazines and strategy guides, action figures, and other related merchandise. In addition, the company operates electronic commerce Websites under the names gamestop.com and ebgames.com, as well as publishes Game Informer, a multiplatform video game magazine in the United States with approximately 1.9 million subscribers. As of April 10, 2006, it operated 4,490 stores in the United States, Australia, Canada, and Europe primarily under the names GameStop and EB Games. The company was founded in 1994 and is headquartered in Grapevine, Texas.
Shares were up 10% after beating analysts' fourth-quarter expectations.
BellwetherReport.com is a leading online research firm for international investors looking to get an edge over their portfolio. Investors seeking the most up to date information on GameStop Corp. are invited to sign up for a free complimentary subscription to www.bellwetherreport.com. No credit card needed!
Video game retailer GameStop beat analysts' fourth-quarter expectations and guided the Street higher for its current quarter and new fiscal year.
Net income for the fourth quarter rose to $129.8 million, or 81 cents a share, from $85 million, or 55 cents a share, a year earlier. Analysts polled by Thomson Financial were expecting earnings of 80 cents a share.
Sales increased 38.2% to $2.3 billion from $1.67 billion a year ago. That compares with Street expectations of $2.12 billion.
On a comparable-store basis, sales increased 26.5% during the fourth quarter.
Shares of GameStop recently soared $3.03, or 10.8%, to $31 in Tuesday trading.
Brisk sales in January of Vivendi's World of Warcraft game and new video game software titles drove results, said GameStop.
For its current first quarter, the company expects comparable- store sales to range from an increase of 12% to 14%, driven by the expected launches of Sony's PlayStation 3 in Europe and Australia, and continued demand for Microsoft Xbox 360 titles.
Earnings for the first quarter are expected to range from 15 cents a share to 16 cents a share, above analysts' expectations of 13 cents a share.
For fiscal 2007, GameStop said sales are likely to grow between 19% and 21%, with comparable-store sales growth of 14% to 16%, backed by a strong release slate of video game titles across all platforms.
The company forecast earnings for the year to range from $1.37 to $1.40. That compares with analysts' expectations of $1.34 a share.
Grapevine, Texas-based GameStop said it will open 500 to 550 stores worldwide in 2007.

Full text: M2 PRESSWIRE-February 23, 2007-bellwetherreport.com: Morning Alert for GameStop Corp. (C)1994-2007 M2 COMMUNICATIONS LTD
GameStop holds the top score in the video game retailing industry. The company is the largest retailer of new and used games, hardware, entertainment software, and accessories through nearly 4,500 outlets in the US and 14 other countries. A majority of sales come from new and used video games; stores carry an average of 1,000 new titles and 4,000 used ones. The company also has e-commerce Web sites (GameStop.com, ebgames.com) and publishes Game Informer, a video game magazine that reaches more than 1.5 million subscribers. The company's 2005 purchase of rival Electronics Boutique doubled GameStop's size.
Shares were down 3% in sector snap.
BellwetherReport.com is a leading online research firm for international investors looking to get an edge over their portfolio. Investors seeking the most up to date information on GameStop Corp. are invited to sign up for a free complimentary subscription to www.bellwetherreport.com. No credit card needed!
Shares of video game publishers were mixed Wednesday following the release of January sales data from the NPD Group, a market research company, showing solid year-over-year growth in software sales.
Analysts reported that based on NPD figures, video game software sales grew 22 percent year-over-year when adjusted for an extra week in the 2007 retail calendar. Sales of games for next-generation systems -- Sony's PlayStation 3, the Nintendo Wii and Microsoft's Xbox 360 -- drove console software sales, said Prudential analyst John McPeake in a note to investors.
Sales of games for handheld systems grew 17 percent when adjusted for the extra week, and sales from Nintendo DS titles more than doubled, according to McPeake.
Activision Inc. and THQ Inc. are growing at a rate above the rest of the industry, while sector leader Electronic Arts Inc. recorded its fourth consecutive quarter of year-over-year sales declines, McPeake noted.
Shares of Activision fell 17 cents to $17.40 in afternoon trading on the Nasdaq Stock Market, and shares of THQ rose 30 cents to $33.89.
McPeake reiterated an "Overweight" rating on Activision and THQ and kept a "Neutral Weight" rating on EA.
"Activision's 'Guitar Hero II' continues to perform significantly above our expectations selling 270,000 units compared to our estimate of 70,000 units during the month of January," McPeake wrote. "Activision titles also continued to perform well on both the PlayStation 3 and Wii and accounted for 16 percent and 10 percent of software sales, respectively." EA's shares rose 66 cents to $52.46 on the Nasdaq.
The Nintendo Wii led hardware sales during the month, reported Bank of America analyst Michael L. Savner.
Wii sales totaled 436,000 units in January, 46 percent more than the PlayStation 2, which sold 299,000 units, Savner wrote. The Xbox 360 was the third best-selling platform with 294,000 units sold.
Microsoft's shares climbed 36 cents to $29.19 on the Nasdaq. Sony's American depositary shares rose 50 cents to $53.04 on the New York Stock Exchange.
Shares of GameStop Corp., the world's biggest video game retailer, rose $1.75, or 3.3 percent, to $55.66 on the NYSE. In the past 52 weeks, the stock has traded between $35.87 and $58.42.

Full text: M2 PRESSWIRE-January 26, 2007-Blue Chip News: GameStop Corp. Added to Bellwether Watch List (C)1994-2007 M2 COMMUNICATIONS LTD
GameStop holds the top score in the video game retailing industry. The company is the largest retailer of new and used games, hardware, entertainment software, and accessories through nearly 4,500 outlets in the US and 14 other countries. A majority of sales come from new and used video games; stores carry an average of 1,000 new titles and 4,000 used ones. The company also has e-commerce Web sites (GameStop.com, ebgames.com) and publishes Game Informer, a video game magazine that reaches more than 1.5 million subscribers. The company's 2005 purchase of rival Electronics Boutique doubled GameStop's size.
Shares were down 4% despite recent boost in electronics retail sales.
BellwetherReport.com is a leading online research firm for international investors looking to get an edge over their portfolio. Investors seeking the most up to date information on GameStop Corp. are invited to sign up for a free complimentary subscription to www.bellwetherreport.com. No credit card needed!
On a year-over-year basis, total retail sales jumped a seasonally adjusted 5.4% in December. However, electronics and appliance stores booked a staggering 15% increase -- the biggest year-over-year increase since the early '90s. That's very bullish news.
Along with electronics stores, sales in several other discretionary retail groups showed solid year-over-year improvement for the month. These included general-merchandise retailers, up 5.4%; furniture and home-furnishings stores, up 7.6%; and restaurants, up 9.3%. When discretionary retail spending pops like that, it clearly signals that consumers' income is robust and flowing nicely. That, in turn, means more cash for MP3 players, home- theater systems and digital cameras, and that's undoubtedly bullish for electronics retailers.
In fact, I wasn't surprised that retail sales at electronics stores led the way in December. The group's major discounting fueled a stellar Black Friday shopping weekend, getting the 2006 holiday shopping season off to a vigorous start. My own trips to the mall confirmed that a flood of Nintendo video-game consoles, digital music players and flat-panel, high-definition TVs was pouring out retailers' doors. However, I don't believe anyone expected the group's sales to improve at a mind-boggling 15% clip.
From a bird's-eye view, the electronics retail group also boasts many outstanding fundamentals, including a $36 billion market cap, a price-to-earnings ratio of 25.1, and a return on equity of 15%. Those numbers are attractive, but here's the best part: The group carries a long-term debt-to-equity ratio of just 0.26. Translation: For every dollar in owners' equity, electronics stores have just 26 cents in debt. That's less than a fifth of the services industry's long-term debt-to-equity ratio of 1.48, and it shows me that the group maintains solid balance sheets, an important factor for any retailer.
GameStop: This retailer of video-game products and PC entertainment software operates 4,490 stores. It has a $4.4 billion market cap and a weekly chart that looks spectacular.

Full text: M2 PRESSWIRE-November 24, 2006-bellwetherreport.com: Fundamental Review for GameStop Corp (C)1994-2006 M2 COMMUNICATIONS LTD
Fundamental Review for GameStop Corp (NYSE:GME)
GameStop holds the top score in the video game retailing industry. The company is the largest retailer of new and used games, hardware, entertainment software, and accessories through nearly 4,500 outlets in the US and 14 other countries. A majority of sales come from new and used video games; stores carry an average of 1,000 new titles and 4,000 used ones. The company also has e-commerce Web sites (GameStop.com, ebgames.com) and publishes Game Informer, a video game magazine that reaches more than 1.5 million subscribers. The company's 2005 purchase of rival Electronics Boutique doubled GameStop's size.
Shares were up 3% after announcing at the third quarter conference call release of "Gears of War".
BellwetherReport.com is a leading online research firm for international investors looking to get an edge over their portfolio. Investors seeking the most up to date information on GameStop Corp are invited to sign up for a free complimentary subscription to www.bellwetherreport.com. No credit card needed!
Leading video-game retailer GameStop on which I've been very bullish in the Breakout Stocks newsletter since mid-July, commented on its third-quarter conference call that the release of "Gears of War" has resulted in a significant increase in Xbox 360 sales. This is a very important data point, as it indicates that gamers have been looking for a reason to buy the Xbox 360, and now they have one. This also benefits software makers like Electronic Arts as the Xbox 360 audience should increase in size nicely over the next few months.

The video game console wars are now in full battle mode thanks to the debut of Nintendo's Wii and the PS3 over the past few days. While the PS3 and the Wii will be available in short supply for the next few months, Sony Nintendo, and Microsoft are nonetheless wholeheartedly scrapping for market share in this latest battle for gaming supremacy. While we continue to like Microsoft for a host of reasons, we recently indicated in an article for subscribers that investors interested in an angle on the console upgrades should consider specialty retailer GameStop . The stock has been volatile since we first broached the subject last month, but thanks to a nice gain today, the stock has advanced about 4% over the last four weeks.

Full text: GameStop Corp. reported a profit for its fiscal third quarter as charges related to the acquisition of Electronics Boutique hurt year- earlier results. For the quarter ended Oct. 28, the Grapevine, Texas, videogame retailer, which was spun off from Barnes & Noble Inc. in 2002, had net income of $13.6 million, or 17 cents a share, compared with a year-earlier net loss of $2.5 million, or four cents a share. Revenue rose 89% to $1.01 billion, helped by the acquisition of Electronics Boutique late in the year-earlier third quarter. Sales at stores open at least a year increased 8.8%. Videogame sales rose 14%, thanks in part to Madden 2007 NFL, Saints Row and Dead Rising. Hardware sales increased 69%, as Microsoft Corp.'s Xbox 360 was released shortly after last year's third quarter. The release of Sony Corp.'s PlayStation 3 and Nintendo Co.'s Wii game systems are seen helping retailers' fourth-quarter results. In 4 p.m. composite trading on the New York Stock Exchange, GameStop shares were up $1.84, or 3.6%, to $53.

Sony Corp. has receded from its days of glory, when the Walkman was the synonym for portable music and PlayStation 2 was the pinnacle of video game consoles, having unseated the mighty Nintendo.
While Sony was once an icon of quality, now its batteries are being recalled as fire hazards, mass production problems are delaying wide release of its much-awaited PlayStation 3, and rivals are outselling its TV sets. Amid all this, the company posted a 71 percent decline in the operating profit of its electronic segment in the most recent fiscal quarter, with overall profit down 94 percent, weighed down among other things by the costs of launching the PS3.
Howard Stringer, Sony's first non-Japanese chief executive, is leading the company in a turnaround plan, but the effort has hit some snags, notably the recall of 9.6 million laptop batteries that has cost the company $429 million so far.
The electronics business, Sony's largest segment, is facing growing competition from the likes of Apple Computer's iPod, Samsung's flat-screen television sets and even Nintendo's upcoming Wii console, which will cost half as much as the cheaper version of the PS3.
Citing problems with mass-producing the PS3's Blu-ray video technology, Sony said in September it will delay the European launch of the console and ship a smaller amount to the U.S. and Japan than originally planned.
The company has maintained it still plans to ship 6 million units worldwide by next March. But Piper Jaffray analyst Anthony Gikas is doubtful -- he expects Sony to fall "well short" of this target, shipping only 3.5 million to 4 million of the consoles.
In October, GameStop Corp., the largest U.S. video game retailer, offered its customers a limited number of slots, at $100 each, to pre-order the PlayStation 3. In some cases, the spots were filled within minutes.
If pre-order trends are any indication, the consoles will likely be snagged up in hours, if not minutes, when they reach the stores, and shortages are widely expected, which should bode well for Nintendo and Microsoft.
A week after announcing the PlayStation 3 shortfall, Sony said it was delaying the launch of its digital music player, NW-S203F, due to the malfunction of a component the company did not specify.
And, in October, Sony postponed the release of LocationFree TV Box LF-Box1, which streams TV programs and movies wirelessly to devices such as portable PlayStation units and Macintosh and Windows- based computers.
Some U.S. investors have sold off the company's shares, which are down 10 percent since the beginning of August.
Despite the bad news, Goldman Sachs analyst Yuri Fujimori recommended buying the company's shares, on weakness, to Japanese investors in a recent note to clients.
Merrill Lynch's Hitoshi Kuriyama, who rates Sony "Sell" said the adverse effects of the battery recall, the growing PlayStation 3- related costs and the risk of a PS3 business failure have already factored in to the company's shares, at least to some extent.
Nonetheless, the analysts predicts some risks for 2007, including the profitability of Sony's TV business, as well as responsibility for the battery recalls.
. The call will be archived for two weeks on GameStop Corp.'s website.

Full text: M2 PRESSWIRE-October 11, 2006-bellwetherreport.com: Bellwether Report.com is Keeping a Close Watch on GameStop Corp. (C)1994-2006 M2 COMMUNICATIONS LTD
The Bellwether Report Takes Notice of GameStop Corp. (Nyse: GME)
GameStop holds the top score in the video game retailing industry. The company is the largest retailer of new and used games, hardware, entertainment software, and accessories through almost 4,500 outlets in the US and 14 other countries. A majority of sales come from new and used video games; stores carry an average of 1,000 new titles and 4,000 used ones. The company also has e-commerce Web sites (GameStop.com, ebgames.com) and publishes Game Informer, a video game magazine that reaches more than 1.5 million subscribers. The company's 2005 purchase of rival Electronics Boutique doubled GameStop's size.
Shares were up 2% after announcing stores are going to start accepting pre-orders for Sony's PlayStation 3.
GameStop and EB Games stores are going to start accepting pre- orders for Sony's PlayStation 3 game console on Tuesday, according to their Web sites.
Due to "extremely limited supply," the stores expect their allocations of what is perhaps the holiday's season's most eagerly anticipated gadget to run out in minutes.
A $100 deposit is required for each order, but even that won't guarantee that a PlayStation 3 will be available when the console goes on sale on Nov. 17, according to the notices, because the stores have no control over production and shipping issues.
The console will be sold in two versions, for $499 and $599. Sony Corp. has said it plans to ship 2 million units by the end of the year.

Per- share earnings fell 21% to 15 cents, as weighted average shares outstanding increased 44% after the $1.44 billion cash-and-stock acquisition of Electronics Boutique in October. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame retail chain posted net income in the quarter ended Jan. 28 of $85 million, or $1.10 a share, up from $34.5 million, or 64 cents a share, in the year-earlier period.

Links: http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2006&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Earnings+More+Than+Double+On+Acquisition+of+Competitor&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Earnings+More+Than+Double+On+Acquisition+of+Competitor&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2006&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Earnings+More+Than+Double+On+Acquisition+of+Competitor&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Earnings+More+Than+Double+On+Acquisition+of+Competitor&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

Full text: GameStop Corp.'s fiscal fourth-quarter profit and sales more than doubled, helped by the October acquisition of rival Electronics Boutique. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame retail chain posted net income in the quarter ended Jan. 28 of $85 million, or $1.10 a share, up from $34.5 million, or 64 cents a share, in the year-earlier period. Sales rose to $1.66 billion from $708.7 million, mainly due to the Electronic Boutique stores. Sales at comparable GameStop stores were slightly lower. GameStop plans to open 400 stores this year and 600 stores in 2007 and 2008. It expects first-quarter same-store sales, or sales at stores open at least a year, to be 7% to 9% lower than a year ago, due mainly to the launch of Sony's PSP hand-held game console in the year-earlier quarter. It expects full-year earnings of $1.83 to $1.93 a share, including 27 cents of stock-based compensation expenses, above forecasts for $1.77 a share by analysts surveyed by Thomson Financial. Shares rose $3.60, or 8.7%, to $45 in New York Stock Exchange 4 p.m. composite trading.

GameStop Corp.: Earnings Guidance Is Raised After Strong December Sales

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]06 Jan 2006: C.11.

http://elib.tcd.ie/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/gamestop-corp-earnings-guidance-is-raised-after/docview/399021765/se-2?accountid=14404

Abstract: GameStop Corp. raised its 2005 earnings guidance after strong December sales. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame retailer now expects to earn $1.75 to $1.78 a share for the full year, above a prior forecast for $1.65 to $1.70 a share. Its shares rose 12%, or $3.86, to $37.31, in 4 p.m. composite trading on the New York Stock Exchange.

Links: http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2006&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Earnings+Guidance+Is+Raised+After+Strong+December+Sales&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Earnings+Guidance+Is+Raised+After+Strong+December+Sales&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2006&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Earnings+Guidance+Is+Raised+After+Strong+December+Sales&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Earnings+Guidance+Is+Raised+After+Strong+December+Sales&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

Full text: GameStop Corp. raised its 2005 earnings guidance after strong December sales. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame retailer now expects to earn $1.75 to $1.78 a share for the full year, above a prior forecast for $1.65 to $1.70 a share. Its shares rose 12%, or $3.86, to $37.31, in 4 p.m. composite trading on the New York Stock Exchange. A shortage of Microsoft Corp.'s XBox 360 game console during the holiday had been expected to lead to a drop in sales of videogames or hardware. But GameStop said the 1.5% drop in comparable store sales, excluding the October acquisition of the Electronics Boutique videogame store chain, was in line with expectations. Bank of America analyst Gary Cooper, who expected comparable sales to decline 8% to 10% in the quarter, said good sales between Christmas and New Year's helped to temper the decline. GameStop said sales of used games, which carry higher margins than new games, were very brisk and customers who turned in used games put store credit or cash toward buying new games.

GameStop Corp.: Third-Quarter Loss Is Posted On Weaker Same-Store Sales

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]30 Nov 2005: 1.

http://elib.tcd.ie/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/gamestop-corp-third-quarter-loss-is-posted-on/docview/398949796/se-2?accountid=14404

Abstract: GameStop Corp. swung to a fiscal third-quarter loss, as same-store sales fell 12%. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame retailer, spun off from Barnes & Noble Inc. last year, posted a loss for the quarter ended Oct. 29 of $2.5 million, or four cents a share, from net income of $12.1 million, or 21 cents a share, a year earlier.

Links: http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2005&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Third-Quarter+Loss+Is+Posted+On+Weaker+Same-Store+Sales&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Third-Quarter+Loss+Is+Posted+On+Weaker+Same-Store+Sales&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2005&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Third-Quarter+Loss+Is+Posted+On+Weaker+Same-Store+Sales&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Third-Quarter+Loss+Is+Posted+On+Weaker+Same-Store+Sales&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

Full text: GameStop Corp. swung to a fiscal third-quarter loss, as same-store sales fell 12%. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame retailer, spun off from Barnes & Noble Inc. last year, posted a loss for the quarter ended Oct. 29 of $2.5 million, or four cents a share, from net income of $12.1 million, or 21 cents a share, a year earlier. Results include costs of $11.9 million related to its $1.44 billion acquisition of Electronics Boutique Holdings Corp., completed in the quarter. Sales rose 28% to $534.2 million from $416.7 million. GameStop said same- store sales fell because of the lack of major new titles, in contrast to last year's third quarter, when "Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas" and "Fable" were released. The company also said November new videogame sales were weaker than expected due to many customers waiting for the launch of Microsoft Corp.'s Xbox 360 and that this trend will continue "to a degree throughout the holiday season." As of 4 p.m. composite trading yesterday on the New York Stock Exchange, GameStop class A shares were at $34.99, off 19 cents.

GameStop Corp. Profit Rises 3% on Solid Sales; Weak Quarterly Outlook Issued

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]19 Aug 2005: A.8.

http://elib.tcd.ie/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/gamestop-corp-profit-rises-3-on-solid-sales-weak/docview/398927105/se-2?accountid=14404

Abstract: GameStop Corp.'s profit rose 3% in the fiscal second quarter despite a 20% increase in sales. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame and entertainment-software retailer posted net income of $7.9 million, or 14 cents a share, up from $7.7 million, or 13 cents, a year earlier.

Links: http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2005&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.+Profit+Rises+3%25+on+Solid+Sales%3B+Weak+Quarterly+Outlook+Issued&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.+Profit+Rises+3%25+on+Solid+Sales%3B+Weak+Quarterly+Outlook+Issued&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2005&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.+Profit+Rises+3%25+on+Solid+Sales%3B+Weak+Quarterly+Outlook+Issued&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.+Profit+Rises+3%25+on+Solid+Sales%3B+Weak+Quarterly+Outlook+Issued&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

Full text: GameStop Corp.'s profit rose 3% in the fiscal second quarter despite a 20% increase in sales. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame and entertainment-software retailer posted net income of $7.9 million, or 14 cents a share, up from $7.7 million, or 13 cents, a year earlier. Results for the latest quarter, which ended July 30, included a $1.1 million write-off of used inventory of the game "Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas," due to a retroactive ratings change by the Entertainment Software Rating Board. The game was given an "adults-only" rating when it was discovered sexually explicit scenes could be accessed through software available online. The company's sales rose to $415.9 million. GameStop said it expects same-store sales, or sales at stores open at least a year, to decrease 8% to 10% in the third quarter because year- earlier sales were driven in part by sales of the "Grand Theft Auto," title. The company expects third-quarter earnings of 18 cents to 20 cents a share.

GameStop Corp.: Profit Soars 55% Amid Growth In Software, Hardware Sales

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]25 May 2005: D.7.

http://elib.tcd.ie/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/gamestop-corp-profit-soars-55-amid-growth/docview/398910066/se-2?accountid=14404

Abstract: GameStop Corp.'s fiscal first-quarter earnings rose 55%, driven by strong performances in both software sales and a resurgent growth in hardware.

Links: http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2005&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Profit+Soars+55%25+Amid+Growth+In+Software%2C+Hardware+Sales&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Profit+Soars+55%25+Amid+Growth+In+Software%2C+Hardware+Sales&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2005&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Profit+Soars+55%25+Amid+Growth+In+Software%2C+Hardware+Sales&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Profit+Soars+55%25+Amid+Growth+In+Software%2C+Hardware+Sales&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

Full text: GameStop Corp.'s fiscal first-quarter earnings rose 55%, driven by strong performances in both software sales and a resurgent growth in hardware. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame and software retailer reported net income of $10.3 million, or 19 cents a share, for the quarter ended April 30, compared with $6.7 million, or 11 cents a share, in the year-earlier period. Sales rose 28% to $474.7 million from $371.7 million. The company said an "extremely successful" launch of Sony Corp.'s PlayStation Portable game player helped to fuel the strong sales volume during the quarter, as sales at stores open at least a year increased 12%. GameStop's videogame software sales rose 21%. GameStop continues to forecast fiscal year earnings of $1.30 to $1.40 a share, without taking into consideration the planned merger with Electronics Boutique Holdings Corp. GameStop shares rose $1.21, or 4.2%, to $29.75 as of 4 p.m. in New York Stock Exchange composite trading.

GameStop Corp.: Fourth-Quarter Net Declines But Revenue Increases 13%

Publication info: Wall Street Journal , Eastern edition; New York, N.Y. [New York, N.Y]24 Mar 2005: A.11.

http://elib.tcd.ie/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/gamestop-corp-fourth-quarter-net-declines-revenue/docview/398910062/se-2?accountid=14404

Abstract: GameStop Corp. reported lower net earnings but better sales for the fiscal fourth quarter, and its shares rose.

Links: http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2005&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Fourth-Quarter+Net+Declines+But+Revenue+Increases+13%25&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Fourth-Quarter+Net+Declines+But+Revenue+Increases+13%25&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

http://resolver.ebscohost.com/openurl?sid=ProQ:wpsa&amp;fmt=journal&amp;genre=article&amp;issn=00999660&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=2005&amp;spage=1&amp;title=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Fourth-Quarter+Net+Declines+But+Revenue+Increases+13%25&amp;atitle=GameStop+Corp.%3A+Fourth-Quarter+Net+Declines+But+Revenue+Increases+13%25&amp;au=&amp;isbn=&amp;jtitle=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;btitle=&amp;id=?t:ac=22336720342E496DPQ/1

Full text: GameStop Corp. reported lower net earnings but better sales for the fiscal fourth quarter, and its shares rose. The Grapevine, Texas, videogame store chain said net income in the quarter ended Jan. 29 fell 13% to $34.5 million, or 64 cents a share, from $39.6 million, or 67 cents a share, in the year-ago quarter. Revenue jumped 13% to $708.7 million. Same-store sales, or sales at stores open at least a year, were essentially flat. The latest period included a charge of $3.3 million, or six cents a share, for an adjustment to lease accounting. GameStop, spun off from Barnes & Noble Inc. last year, said it expects earnings growth on higher revenue in the current fiscal year amid continued demand for Sony Corp.'s slimmer Playstation 2 console and the U.S. introduction of the PlayStation Portable game player. Shares of GameStop were up $2.63, or 13%, at $22.12, in 4 p.m. New York Stock Exchange composite trading.

Research and Markets: GAMESTOP CORP(GME) - Quantitative Valuation Report

Publication info: M2 Presswire ; Coventry [Coventry]27 Feb 2003: 1.

http://elib.tcd.ie/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/wire-feeds/research-markets-gamestop-corp-gme-quantitative/docview/443838442/se-2?accountid=14404

Abstract: Choosing the first option will prompt PortfolioAdvisor to create an aggressive yet risky portfolio. Choosing the second option will prompt PortfolioAdvisor to search for a conservative mix of stocks that will seek to preserve capital. Choosing the third option will prompt PortfolioAdvisor to create a balanced portfolio that will seek to both maximize potential gains and minimize potential losses. Once you have specified an investment objective, PortfolioAdvisor will utilize our forecasting models to estimate future returns for the individual stocks in your portfolio. PortfolioAdvisor will then examine tens of thousands of possible capital allocation plans distributed across the stocks of your choice. From the results of these simulations, PortfolioAdvisor will identify and display the most favorable stock allocation for your portfolio. Additionally, PortfolioAdvisor will inform you of the exact number of shares to buy or sell of each stock so that the resulting portfolio will maximize your chances of maximizing gain, minimizing loss, or both.

Full text: M2 PRESSWIRE-27 February 2003-Research and Markets: GAMESTOP CORP(GME) - Quantitative Valuation Report (C)1994-2003 M2 COMMUNICATIONS LTD
Company Name - GAMESTOP CORP
Now you, as an individual investor or investment professional, can have access to the same tools used by equity fund and portfolio managers as they deal with billions of dollars in assets every business day. Our ongoing cooperative research program, involving economists and financial theorists at Yale University and our own development team, has forged a solid bridge between the academic world and the marketplace. Thus armed with the freshest concepts and ideas, the ValuEngine team tests new theories and works out practical applications for them. We can say without fear of contradiction that there is no asset valuation and forecasting system in use today that is the equal of ValuEngine.

Independent, numbers-based, objective Equity Research
Use this report to help to :
- Optimize your equity portfolio for the best risk/return ratio.
- Forecast equity portfolio's value next year.
- Find a fair value for stocks and forecast their future prospects.
- Determine the chances of gain or loss on current holdings.
- Find momentum & volatility ranks for stocks.
"Yale finance professor Dr. Zhiwu Chen has done an excellent job of transforming academic research and rigorous mathematics into a practical investing tool. The valuation model combines 12-month trailing EPS, consensus analyst estimates, and the 30-year Treasury yield to come up with a fair value price for any stock. Then its forecast model uses common market trends such as momentum and price reversals, and runs simulations to determine the most probable price outcomes over three years." - Forbes
Note on the Models used to create the reports:
These company reports employ many proprietary models, which were adapted from innovative concepts in finance theory generated both in academia and from Wall Street practice. Each of the four ValuEngine models represents the state-of-the-art in valuation, forecasting technologies:
1) The VE Stock Valuation Model 2) The VE Stock Forecast Model 3) The VE Portfolio Advisor Model 4) The VE Portfolio Forecast Model
The ValuEngine Stock Valuation Model
The ValuEngine Stock Valuation Model was derived from the recent research and findings of Dr. Zhiwu Chen, Professor of Finance, Yale University, and his co-authors. The model is more sophisticated than traditional valuation models and outperforms its peers by employing a three-factor approach to stock valuation. Fundamental variables such as a company's trailing 12-month Earnings-Per-Share (EPS), the analyst consensus estimate of the company's future 12-month EPS, and the 30-year Treasury yield are all combined and used to create a more accurate reflection of a company's fair value. Armed with these framework features, the Model then paints a detailed picture of a company's fair value, which is represented by the "model price."
The ValuEngine Stock Forecast Model
The predictive variables used in the forecasting models include both proprietary and well-established forecasting variables derived from credible financial research studies and publications. They use a distinct forecasting model for each forecasting horizon and every industry. The forecasting models capture, among other things, several important tendencies that stock prices consistently exhibit: Short-term price reversals Intermediate-term momentum continuation Long-term price reversals. They then apply the most advanced statistical/econometric techniques to ensure that the stock return forecasts are as reliable as possible. In addition, they have a realistic econometric model for assessing a stock's and a portfolio's future return prospects. This econometric model involves running thousands of simulations to estimate the probability of a double in stock price as well as the probability of meeting and exceeding any given investment target by a stock or a portfolio of stocks.
The ValuEngine Portfolio Forecast Model
The PortfolioForecast tool arrives at projections by utilizing forecasting models to estimate future returns for the individual stocks in a portfolio. After computing the future return forecasts for each stock, they then run thousands of concurrent simulations for all of the stocks in a given portfolio (subject to various econometric requirements). The thousands of simulated price paths created by this process form the basis for the PortfolioForecast projections. Finally, the PortfolioForecast tool calculates the most likely return forecast from the thousands of simulated outcomes.
The ValuEngine Portfolio Advisor Model
The ValuEngine PortfolioAdvisor enables you to specify the following portfolio objectives: Maximize the chance of meeting or exceeding an investment target; Minimize the chance of loss; Both of the above.
Choosing the first option will prompt PortfolioAdvisor to create an aggressive yet risky portfolio. Choosing the second option will prompt PortfolioAdvisor to search for a conservative mix of stocks that will seek to preserve capital. Choosing the third option will prompt PortfolioAdvisor to create a balanced portfolio that will seek to both maximize potential gains and minimize potential losses. Once you have specified an investment objective, PortfolioAdvisor will utilize our forecasting models to estimate future returns for the individual stocks in your portfolio. PortfolioAdvisor will then examine tens of thousands of possible capital allocation plans distributed across the stocks of your choice. From the results of these simulations, PortfolioAdvisor will identify and display the most favorable stock allocation for your portfolio. Additionally, PortfolioAdvisor will inform you of the exact number of shares to buy or sell of each stock so that the resulting portfolio will maximize your chances of maximizing gain, minimizing loss, or both.
Back Testing
Every valuation, forecasting, and advisory model has been extensively back-tested in the United States, Hong Kong, and Taiwan equities markets.
The investment performance of each model has been proven to exceed that of many well-known stock-picking styles.

Full text: NEW YORK -- GameStop Corp., the video game and software unit of Barnes & Noble Inc., filed an expected registration for an initial public offering, according to a document filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission on Friday.
GameStop, of Grapevine, Texas, operates 990 stores under such names as GameStop, Babbage's, Software Etc. and FuncoLand. The company intends to sell as much as $325 million of Class A common stock in an IPO planned for October or November.
After the offering, Barnes & Noble would retain a majority stake in GameStop. Barnes & Noble would own 100% of the Class B stock. Each share of Class B would have 10 votes, while Class A would have one vote per share. The document didn't disclose the price or number of shares to be offered. GameStop said it will use about $250 million of the proceeds to repay some of the debt it owes to Barnes & Noble, as well as for working capital and general corporate purposes.
Salomon Smith Barney, a unit of Citigroup Inc., and Swiss banking group UBS AG's UBS Warburg unit will serve as the offering's underwriters. In New York Stock Exchange composite trading Friday at 4 p.m., Barnes & Noble shares rose 31 cents to $42.28.
